  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5554729a-bb73-4098-a2e0-95ab130b37d3'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer4892756313045554683">Sixteen-year-old Janelle Tenner is used to having a lot of responsibility. She balances working as a lifeguard in San Diego with an intense academic schedule.   <span id="freeText4892756313045554683" style="display:none">Sixteen-year-old Janelle Tenner is used to having a lot of responsibility. She balances working as a lifeguard in San Diego with an intense academic schedule. Janelle's mother is bipolar, and her dad is a workaholic FBI agent, which means Janelle also has to look out for her younger brother, Jared.<br /><br />And that was before she died... and is brought back to life by Ben Michaels, a mysterious, alluring loner from her high school. When she discovers a strange clock that seems to be counting down to the earth's destruction, Janelle learns she has twenty-four days to figure out how to stop the clock and save the planet.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260224340" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/260224340?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=april">april</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=poc">poc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=sci-fi-or-futuristic">sci-fi-or-futuristic</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer260224340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6493032920617519339">The end of the world is coming! When a book begins with the heroine getting hit by a truck and killed in the first chapter, you know you’re in for a good time. 17-year-old Janelle Tenner somehow wakes up miraculously unhurt, however, and staring into the eyes of a boy she barely knows. In the 24 days that follow, she has to figure out what Ben has to do with her strange revival, as well as how her FBI agent father’s investigation into a series of unidentified burn victims might tie into her own </span>
  <span id="freeText6493032920617519339" style="display:none">The end of the world is coming! When a book begins with the heroine getting hit by a truck and killed in the first chapter, you know you’re in for a good time. 17-year-old Janelle Tenner somehow wakes up miraculously unhurt, however, and staring into the eyes of a boy she barely knows. In the 24 days that follow, she has to figure out what Ben has to do with her strange revival, as well as how her FBI agent father’s investigation into a series of unidentified burn victims might tie into her own story...and the fate of her entire world.<br /><br />This sci-fi mystery took me by surprise, in a very good way. While I go into all YA novels with an open mind, particularly when the premise is as intriguing as this one, I admit to a certain degree of ennui after slogging through so many tedious paranormal romances that don’t add very much to the genre. Despite its somewhat ambiguous blurb, it’s nice to find that this is not PNR at all, although I think it will definitely still appeal to fans of that genre. While there discussions of quantum physics, viral engineering, and various other interesting theories, the book is written in a very accessible and entertaining way. The story does take some cues from X-Files, Fringe, Veronica Mars, and a host of other sources, but I don’t think anyone but the most hard-core fans of those shows will nitpick with the influences that are found here.<br /><br /><b>Things I really enjoyed:</b><br /><br /><b>Janelle’s leafing through her father’s case files:</b> I’m the type to do this too, especially if I found reports of severe radiation poisoning that resulted in gelatinous, melty humans. Let me say that again: <i>gelatinous melty humans</i>. :D<br /><br /><b>Janelle’s dad:</b> We really only get to know him much later in the book, but her relationship with him was plausibly complicated, with the confusing combination of anger and frustration and love and guilt and regret that starts to surface when you're the heroine's age.<br /><br /><b>A romance that eventually grew on me:</b> I was relatively indifferent to Ben and Janelle as a couple at first, but I gradually warmed up to their relationship. The first cute moment came with grape soda, and then their attraction grew into a keen connection that I became invested in.<br /><br /><b>Realistic family drama and setting:</b> Janelle’s father is a workaholic and her mother is bipolar and unreliable, so it’s up to her to parent herself and her younger brother. I thought the family dynamic was well done, and it added an interesting complexity and tension to Janelle’s situation. I also liked the way Janelle’s school life was a part of the book, because it’s such a big part of being a teenager and yet often gets ignored in YA.<br /><br /><b>Things that could have been smoothed out a bit more:</b><br /><br /><b>There’s a lot crammed into 450 pages:</b> While I appreciate the fact that this isn’t not a sketchy wham-bam-thank-you-ma’am kind of book, some of the subplots did seem a bit superfluous. If the ex-boyfriend, subplot about rape, etc. were more compelling, perhaps I wouldn’t have felt that way, but as it is, I think the book easily could have rid itself of 100 pages without losing anything vital.<br /><br /><b>Fairly unremarkable secondary characters:</b> Aside from Janelle and Ben, Janelle’s dad, and her ex-boyfriend Nick, most of the other characters blended together for me.<br /><br /><b>The structure:</b> the choice to break up the story into segments corresponding with the mysterious countdown is a good one, but I’m not sure it was necessary to have so many short breakdowns, to the point that essentially each change in scene merits its own chapter. Because the story also flits back and forth as it fills us in on backstory, there were occasions when it also disrupted the flow of the story. We’re in the middle of a tense scene at the climax of the book, for example, when we suddenly step out of the action to a flashback of Halloween, which could have easily been included elsewhere.<br /><br /><b>A couple of overly dramatic gun-brandishing moments</b>, one of which I suppose could be explained away as the character’s extreme agitation after finding out upsetting news, but it’s a little harder to look the other way when it’s being done by an FBI agent.<br /><br /><b>Writing technique occasionally trumping story:</b> this goes back to the structure thing, although there are other moments when I felt a little jolted out of the engrossing plot because of a line that is included for irony or affect. For example, Ben’s unorthodox way of telling Janelle how he feels about her, “I fucking love you,” is strangely commandeered by someone else during an important scene towards the end of the book. In my opinion, the emotional punch of a poignant moment was interrupted and diminished because of that inclusion.<br /><br />Despite these criticisms (and my dislike for the Heroes-like tagline), I very much enjoyed this book, which is the first one in a planned series. While I wasn’t really surprised by any of the twists and it wasn’t a story that moved me strongly enough to tears, I did find that the way the author explores the aftermath of grief and separation seemed very true to life, particularly in Janelle’s conflicting feelings and the heavy weight of her responsibilities. That strong opening scene is also bookended with a fantastic ending, one that leaves the door open for the story continue, but also feels emotionally satisfying—even if it is extremely wistful, bittersweet one.<br /><br /><i>Unraveling</i> is a great blend of science fiction, mystery, and romance with solid writing and a memorable story, and this debut author is definitely one to watch.<br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2012/04/unraveling-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>. An advance copy was provided by the publisher.</i><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6493032920617519339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_286629041" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/286629041" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/286629041?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286629041" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9466614564110304827">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/03/unraveling-by-elizabeth-norris.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/>2.5 stars <br/><br/>When I look back at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12157365.Unraveling__Unraveling___1_' title='Unraveling (Unraveling, #1) by Elizabeth Norris' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unraveling</a>, the first word that comes to mind is "calculated."<br/><br/>I read a fair number of commercial genre fiction and I am quite used to certain themes, plots and character archetypes being recycled over and over and over and over. It does not bother me, in general. But <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12157365.Unraveling__Unraveling___1_' title='Unraveling (Unraveling, #1) by Elizabeth Norris' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unraveling</a> was the first book that made me think, while reading it, that it had been written off of a checklist of what is currently "in" and sells well in YA market. I do not</span>
  <span id="freeText9466614564110304827" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/03/unraveling-by-elizabeth-norris.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br />2.5 stars <br /><br />When I look back at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12157365.Unraveling__Unraveling___1_" title="Unraveling (Unraveling, #1) by Elizabeth Norris" rel="nofollow noopener">Unraveling</a>, the first word that comes to mind is "calculated."<br /><br />I read a fair number of commercial genre fiction and I am quite used to certain themes, plots and character archetypes being recycled over and over and over and over. It does not bother me, in general. But <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12157365.Unraveling__Unraveling___1_" title="Unraveling (Unraveling, #1) by Elizabeth Norris" rel="nofollow noopener">Unraveling</a> was the first book that made me think, while reading it, that it had been written off of a checklist of what is currently "in" and sells well in YA market. I do not even have energy (nor a desire) to harp on how much of this novel is tediously familiar. Just a few notes:<br /><br /> 1. Opening: the hero saves the heroine from dying.<br /> 2. Romance: 50% instalove (see #1)/ 50% I-have-loved-you-forever. Escalates to I-can't-live-without-you in a matter of 2-3 weeks.<br /> 3. The heroine is "strong" - smart, good student, knows how stand up for herself, family caretaker, family problems, dark traumatic incident in her past of sexual nature.<br /> 4. The hero is "good" - sensitive, caring, saves the heroine on multiple occasions, with floppy hair he is constantly running his hands through, crooked smile, with dark secret, fixes motorcycles, hides his smarts under a stoner persona.<br /> 5. School: a class that is conveniently designed for the hero and the heroine to banter on a very intimate level, encouraged by the teacher.<br /> 6. Other stock characters: stoners, slutty mean girls, stupid jocks, the heroine's best male friend (possibly gay? unclear).<br /> 7. Sleeping chastely in the same bed? Yes.<br /><br /> etc., etc,...<br /><br />Is it really that hard for writers to break away from the same old, same old? Or is this what publishers are consciously and actively seeking out? Something that fits the mold?<br /><br />There are a few saving graces, however, that barely keep <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12157365.Unraveling__Unraveling___1_" title="Unraveling (Unraveling, #1) by Elizabeth Norris" rel="nofollow noopener">Unraveling</a> from the 1-star abyss, in my case, and, apparently, elevate this book to the level of a favorite, for other readers.<br /><br />First, it appears the author of the novel went out of her way to make sure to put all positive qualities into her characters and situations. There is no promoting of unhealthy relationships, abusive behavior, doormatedness and so on. The main characters even give small lectures along the way on the matters of dating, dangers of motorcycle riding, drunk driving, honorable way of hacking into the school records, etc.<br /><br />Second, while I was not at any point enamored with the characters, I still thought the book was a very brisk read. The writing has a sense of urgency to it. The chapters are very short and represent a countdown to a very important, possibly life-threatening event. So you just tear through these pages, like there is no tomorrow.<br /><br />Third, this novel starts out as a paranormal (after all, the hero magically brings the heroine back from death), but eventually turns into a science fiction story (SF is on the rise, people!, that is why it is in this book, I am betting). Several very positive reviews of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12157365.Unraveling__Unraveling___1_" title="Unraveling (Unraveling, #1) by Elizabeth Norris" rel="nofollow noopener">Unraveling</a> I have read call this SF bend unique, and readers seem to like it a lot.<br /><br />But I beg to differ here. Maybe because I do read a lot of SF and I have very recently read another (much better) YA SF with the same ideas <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11291920.Planesrunner__Everness__1_" title="Planesrunner (Everness #1) by Ian McDonald" rel="nofollow noopener">Planesrunner</a>) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but I cannot seriously call <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12157365.Unraveling__Unraveling___1_" title="Unraveling (Unraveling, #1) by Elizabeth Norris" rel="nofollow noopener">Unraveling</a> a good SF novel. There is hardly any science in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12157365.Unraveling__Unraveling___1_" title="Unraveling (Unraveling, #1) by Elizabeth Norris" rel="nofollow noopener">Unraveling</a>, the SF "hook" goes generally undeveloped. As for how much science there is actually in this book, I would say close to zero. You can expect nothing more, if the characters in this novel say: "I've spent hours going over it in my head. I was wrong when I told A. no one else knows the science. Both B. and C. know the science..." (identities concealed to avoid spoilers). So that is the extent of scientific knowledge in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12157365.Unraveling__Unraveling___1_" title="Unraveling (Unraveling, #1) by Elizabeth Norris" rel="nofollow noopener">Unraveling</a>. There are no specifics, just that elusive "science" that characters "know" and "do."<br /><br />Readers less jaded and less demanding are likely to enjoy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12157365.Unraveling__Unraveling___1_" title="Unraveling (Unraveling, #1) by Elizabeth Norris" rel="nofollow noopener">Unraveling</a> more. The book's pace is snappy and the story itself packs all the "right" elements. But there is just no originality in it, no life in its characters, no true inspiration behind it. An aggregate of bluntly "popular" pieces carefully put together. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9466614564110304827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer8241581867179824553">My name is Janelle, I'm the star of this book. I'm super smart. I am way above all these social misfits in this book, in fact, they are so beneath me, I just call them "stoners" or whatever else I see fit. My boyfriend Nick is a loser, I'm just with him because I felt sorry for him and when he smiles, he is soooooo devilishly handsome. I'm going to lie to avoid him, and use my friend Alex to come up with excuses to stay away from Nick. <br/><br/>Oh yes, don't forget Alex. He's my super smart best friend w</span>
  <span id="freeText8241581867179824553" style="display:none">My name is Janelle, I'm the star of this book. I'm super smart. I am way above all these social misfits in this book, in fact, they are so beneath me, I just call them "stoners" or whatever else I see fit. My boyfriend Nick is a loser, I'm just with him because I felt sorry for him and when he smiles, he is soooooo devilishly handsome. I'm going to lie to avoid him, and use my friend Alex to come up with excuses to stay away from Nick. <br /><br />Oh yes, don't forget Alex. He's my super smart best friend who happens to live next door. We are so smart that some gravitational force caused the two super smart (and I mean brilliant) people to end up right next door to each other. It was a brilliant move in terms of storytelling. <br /><br />Even though I'm super smart, any future bad behavior on my part, we can blame my mom. My mom is bipolar, and she has ups and downs faster than a roller coaster, so if I'm not that stable, we'll blame her, because her bipolar is the perfect textbook bipolar that helps set this story up as well.<br /><br />Let's not forget about Ben. He's a stoner but he doesn't smell like smoke so I think he's not a real stoner. Because stoners always smell like smoke. Remember, I'm brilliant, and I make brilliant deductions.<br /><br />But you'll never be as brilliant as me since you stopped reading. Oh well, I'll be super smart, and brilliant without you.</span>

<div id="review_292354842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292354842" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292354842?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007460212" href="/book/show/12924288-unravelling">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=are-you-kidding-me">are-you-kidding-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=amazing-writing">amazing-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2012">arc-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=highly-anticipating-2012">highly-anticipating-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=role-models">role-models</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292354842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5084550656691099715"><b>
  <i>Update 04/17/12: Stop by <a href='http://thenocturnallibrary.blogspot.com/2012/04/guest-post-by-elizabeth-norris-author.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Nocturnal Library</a> to read a guest post by Elizabeth Norris and enter for a chance to win a hardcover copy of Unraveling.</i>
</b><br/><br/>I never give five stars easily, but I'd give this book ten if I could.<br/><br/>I always feel this strange sense of accomplishment when I discover a book I can add to my all-time favorites. There aren’t many books that mean so much to me and that I keep going back to over and over again. I take that short list and adding books to it very seriously. Theref</span>
  <span id="freeText5084550656691099715" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Update 04/17/12: Stop by <a href="http://thenocturnallibrary.blogspot.com/2012/04/guest-post-by-elizabeth-norris-author.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Nocturnal Library</a> to read a guest post by Elizabeth Norris and enter for a chance to win a hardcover copy of Unraveling.</i>
</b><br /><br />I never give five stars easily, but I'd give this book ten if I could.<br /><br />I always feel this strange sense of accomplishment when I discover a book I can add to my all-time favorites. There aren’t many books that mean so much to me and that I keep going back to over and over again. I take that short list and adding books to it very seriously. Therefore, I needed to give myself some time before reviewing this because I was afraid that my initial reaction was entirely emotional and that my enthusiasm will drop once I calm down. I slept on it, I finished a very different book by one of my favorite authors, but none of that changed how I feel. If anything, I am now convinced more than ever that I found something truly special in Unravelling (that’s two Ls in the UK edition, only one in the US). <br /><br />Janelle Tanner is living with her parents and her younger brother, working as a lifeguard at the beach and dating a gorgeous and extremely popular high school senior, Nick. Her life looks perfect on the outside, but on the inside, her mother is bipolar and needs to be taken care of, and her father, no matter how wonderful, has a job that’s keeping him away most of the time. He’s the head of counterintelligence in the FBI’s office in San Diego, and he just got a case that’s driving him and the other agents crazy. An explosive device has been discovered and it’s counting down days, but no matter how many experts they bring in, no one has any idea what it is or how to disarm it. As if that’s not enough, unidentifiable bodies, almost completely melted from radiation, are suddenly showing up everywhere. One of these bodies was found in the car that hit Janelle on her way home from work. She seemed more or less fine after the accident, but what no one knows, what no one would ever believe her, is that she died when the car hit her, and a stoner kid from her school, Ben Michaels, brought her back to life and healed her. Who is Ben? Where are all the bodies coming from? What’s going to happen when the countdown finally hits zero? Is it all somehow connected? Janelle and her best friend Alex always enjoyed ‘borrowing’ her father’s case files from his home office and discussing his cases, but this time, they may be in over their heads. <br /><br />Elizabeth Norris’ writing is flawless. It doesn’t draw attention to itself, but it keeps you engaged and controls your emotions in a way that doesn’t make you feel manipulated. Unravelling is action-packed from start to finish, but that doesn’t mean that it lacks depth. It was truly heartbreaking, and I gave myself a headache from all the crying. If you think this is just another YA novel, think again, because Elizabeth Norris pulled no punches. She kept surprising me on every page, and each time I thought I had it all figured out, she did something entirely unexpected. It was like watching the awesome first season of Fringe all over again, but with a likeable heroine instead of Olivia. <br /><br />Don’t you just love a girl who doesn’t spend all her time consciously making one mistake after another because she lacks the backbone to do the right thing? That’s our Janelle for you, a girl who knows exactly what she wants and doesn’t hesitate to make it happen. She’d been a victim once and she has no intention of being one ever again, so she thinks hard about every choice she makes and doesn’t allow herself to be influenced by anyone else’s opinion. She’s my new character I want to be best friends with. I always expect YA heroines to disappoint me sooner or later, because they almost always do, but with Janelle, that never happened. I can count on the fingers of one hand the characters that impressed me as much as she did.<br /><br />(Did you guys notice how I avoided writing about Ben as much as possible? I'm trying to be serious here and I don't think gushing about that boy would help my cause much. But rest assured, he IS perfect.)<br /><br />I think I’ve made my opinion pretty clear: I cannot recommend this highly enough. I can’t wait to find out how other people will feel about it. Do yourselves a favor and preorder this one, you won’t regret it. <br /><br /><i>A copy of this book was kindly provided by the publisher, HarperCollins UK, for review purposes.</i><br /><br />Also posted at <a href="http://thenocturnallibrary.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Nocturnal Library</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5084550656691099715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_353146252" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/353146252" />
    <a title="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3854740-christina-ensconced-in-lit"><img alt="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372018610p2/3854740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/353146252?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" href="/user/show/3854740-christina-ensconced-in-lit">Christina (Ensconced in Lit)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer353146252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5936363138128779866">After enduring several duds on my list, I decided to treat myself to a book I've been dying to read for a while. I'm not sure what I was expecting, but I loved this book!<br/><br/>Unraveling by Elizabeth Norris is about Janelle, a teenaged girl who seems just like any other ordinary teen, until she dies... and is brought back to life by a boy she's never noticed. She believes she has been given a second chance and is determined to live life to the fullest. But she also has a streak of curiosity and wants </span>
  <span id="freeText5936363138128779866" style="display:none">After enduring several duds on my list, I decided to treat myself to a book I've been dying to read for a while. I'm not sure what I was expecting, but I loved this book!<br /><br />Unraveling by Elizabeth Norris is about Janelle, a teenaged girl who seems just like any other ordinary teen, until she dies... and is brought back to life by a boy she's never noticed. She believes she has been given a second chance and is determined to live life to the fullest. But she also has a streak of curiosity and wants to find out Ben's secret in addition to helping her FBI agent dad solve a case about several dead people who have apparently been killed by a healthy dose of radiation. To make matters worse, her father has found a device that is ticking down to a certain doomsday. Will Janelle be able to figure out the answers before the clock reaches zero?<br /><br />If I could describe this book in a tagline, it would be Veronica Mars meets Fringe. The first 60% of the book, while beautifully written, doesn't have a ton of surprises. Instead, I would say it is almost an homage of all the wonderful books, movies, and shows that have come before it. In addition to the two I mentioned above, there are shout-outs to X-files, Ender's Game, Before I Fall, and some plot twists that are similar to the teen series and show Roswell. The characters are terrific-- Janelle is a wonderful protagonist-- spunky and smart. Her best friend, Alex, may be my favorite character. Ben is a fascinating love interest, and even though when I realize logically that the way he knows Janelle is kind of creepy, Norris masterfully weaves the story to make it seem normal. The pacing of the story is great, and the last 40% of the book approaches unknown territory, which makes it fun to keep guessing. <br /><br />Overall, a terrific addition to the small but persistent genre of YA science fiction with a great protagonist and plot twists-- I can't wait to pick up the next installment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5936363138128779866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272159565" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272159565?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062103758" href="/book/show/13425392-unraveling">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ari by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=arc-galley-or-author">arc-galley-or-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=rereading-material">rereading-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=beloved">beloved</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272159565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15672570186056370376">Elizabeth Norris, <i>I fucking love you!</i><br/><br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/elizabeth-norris/review-unraveling.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368992i/721636.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>If I had to describe this book in only one word I would say “incredible”, but if I had more words to play around I would say something along this lines:<br/>“Mind-blowing, heartbreaking with a pinch of humor and an action/suspense overdose... all in the best possible way. Keep both eyes on it when it comes out! And be assured - this is a hell of a great book!“<br/><br/>And if I had even more words to use.. well, you should sit down as I have many things to say about thi</span>
  <span id="freeText15672570186056370376" style="display:none">Elizabeth Norris, <i>I fucking love you!</i><br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/elizabeth-norris/review-unraveling.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368992i/721636.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>If I had to describe this book in only one word I would say “incredible”, but if I had more words to play around I would say something along this lines:<br>“Mind-blowing, heartbreaking with a pinch of humor and an action/suspense overdose... all in the best possible way. Keep both eyes on it when it comes out! And be assured - this is a hell of a great book!“<br><br>And if I had even more words to use.. well, you should sit down as I have many things to say about this book.<br><br><b>
  <i>My Thoughts:</i>
</b><br>Define love: <em>An intense feeling of deep affection;</em><br>Define adoration: <em>A feeling of profound love &amp; admiration;<br></em>…Close, but these words are simply not enough.<br><br>Unraveling is probably one of the best books in 2012, and yes, I realize it’s only April.<br>It's funny because I read Elizabeth’s blog and I noticed that her favorite book is "<a title="Review: On the Jellicoe Road" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/on-the-jellicoe-road-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Jellicoe Road</a>", and (…take a guess, you have one chance!) that's mine too. Next to it I put “<a title="Review: Graffiti Moon" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/cath-crowley/graffiti-moon-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Graffiti Moon</a>” last year and, in 2012 I’m adding, “Unraveling” to the list as well.<br><br>I don't remember the last time I’ve been so lost into a story.<br>I simply couldn't put it down and I was turning pages like crazy wanting to see what happens next, but in the same time not wanting to reach the ending.<br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/kiss%20at%20school%20anime/AngelsHearts/anime-kiss.jpg?o=10" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368992i/721637.png" alt="" width="217" height="246" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There is this mixture of feelings this book gave me. There were happy moments and really heartbreaking ones, there were moments when my heart was speeding dangerously, and there were moments when I didn’t realize that I was holding my breath until Janelle realized just the same thing:<br><blockquote>"I let go of a breath I didn't know I was holding"</blockquote><br>This book will probably make you too want to write in italics, bold, caps lock, using way too many exclamation points and filling the review with tons of animated gifs showing your excitement (and I don't even like gifs <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[because they are the reason why images appear no longer in our homepage feed on Goodreads <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>). But don't worry, I’ll keep this urge in check for your sake and I’ll let my feeling flow without hurting your eyes.<br><br>I'll have to hold back a lot in order not to spoil this story, but at the ending all I could think was how amazing this book really was.<br><br>It seemed like the author snooped into my entire ‘favorites’ shelf, took all the best things from the books I loved and put them into this wonderful story. More than that, all the things I don't usually like in YA were transformed in such way that they worked wonders in this book.<br><br><b>
  <em>What I liked:</em>
</b><br><strong>The main character</strong><br><a href="http://zindy.deviantart.com/art/Time-187438348" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368992i/721638.jpg" alt="" width="287" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Janelle is independent, sarcastic, confident, she can always rely on her best friend but she can handle it all by her herself too. She is the kind of character you like to read about. Yes, she makes mistakes and her snooping around gets her in trouble more than once, but at the end of the day you will always be proud of her.<br><br>The thing is that she knows she died in the car accident and that somehow a boy brought her back to life - she doesn't know why or how, but she will get to the bottom of it, and when that happens maybe she will find out more about her dad's new case that seems somehow related to her death.<br>She has questions, she doesn’t understand some things, she doesn’t know whom to trust, but she doesn’t give up. The countdown is not stopping, and she has only one chance to find the truth and maybe try to change some things in the way.<br><br><strong>The love story</strong><br><br><a href="http://simoren.deviantart.com/art/Lovely-Complex-Sunset-79163776" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368992i/721639.jpg" alt="" width="221" height="221" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>Oh, it is sweet - but it doesn't take over the action. There are more important things that both Janelle and Ben have to do. Still they share some cute moments and I like how their story is portrayed: it happens to know someone for a very long time but not pay attention to that person until one day when you see everything with other eyes. Sometimes you never know when in the world did you fall in love but sometimes you know the exact moment when everything changed, the moment when you two locked eyes and it felt like for the very first time.<br><blockquote>"My goal is always going to be to get home." Home. For him, it's a place I don't belong.</blockquote><br><strong>The action<br></strong>All those melting bodies (and I am not saying more about them), and all those turnarounds, all the suspense with the clock dangerously counting down to 0 - all those will make you feel like you are watching a movie unfold in front of your eyes. There are paranormal and science-fiction elements, there is drama, there is a lot of action to keep you more than entertained, there is a cute love story that will trap your heart from the very beginning... Everything fits so perfectly together, every character has a purpose, and you will mourn every single loss until the very last page and long after that.<br><br><strong>The Friendship<br></strong>I liked so much the friendship between Janelle and Alex. And if you are wondering - no, this time there is no love-triangle, there is nothing to make your eyes roll in this department. There is trust, and devotion, and love but in a different way, a non-romantic type. That kind of love that would make you do anything for your friends (you’ll bail them from everything, you will go to the end of the world for them, you will keep their secrets and help them out no matter how mad you are at each other). True friendship, that is.<br><br><strong>More:</strong><br>I could never fit into this review all the things the book is about and I won't even try - but it felt 'real' in a way most books never do. There were family issues, and social issues, there were friendships forming and breaking, there were murder investigations and paranormal activities, but also subjects close to our day-by-day life (as school and grief)... Also there are so many other things I would like to talk about, but I have to hold them back. Maybe after you read this book, we'll talk more about it, maybe then we will share our thoughts about all that happened in this book, all the mysteries, all the turnarounds and how much that ending killed us a bit and made us want to live in a world where the next book is already out.<br><br>So what I am saying with all this babbling is that I loved this story, and I think that most of you will do as well. I think that Elizabeth is a great writer, and I am holding my breath for the next book to come out. And I think that I've said enough..too much talking and less reading - not good, not good.<br><br>Happy midnight reading!<br><br><em>Book source: Thanks to one of my great book friends for allowing me to read an Advanced Copy</em><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/elizabeth-norris/review-unraveling.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/elizabeth-norris/review-unraveling.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br><br>Re-read in 2013.<br>I still enjoyed deeply this story - even though now the turnarounds didn't take me by surprise and I didn't feel like holding my breath all the time (because I knew what was coming my way). <br>I wished for the romance to feel less like rushed, but now that I know Ben better and I remember Janelle seeing herself through his eyes it kind of make sense. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15672570186056370376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_297813484" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297813484" />
    <a title="Megs ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5691412-megs"><img alt="Megs ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587306329p2/5691412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/297813484?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megs ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megs ♥" href="/user/show/5691412-megs">Megs ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Megs ♥ by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=z-2012-reads">z-2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer297813484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13698821339882786692"><br/>This book has made a splash amongst YA reviewers lately, so I had to make sure I had this read before its release on the 24th. Also, the synopsis saying "24 meets the X Files" made me very interested.<br/><br/><br/>Janelle is a 17 year old girl who seems to have the perfect life. Nice, fun job as a lifeguard on the beach, super popular hottie boyfriend, cute little brother and more. She also has a dad that works for the FBI. One day when she is going through his files she discovers a file that says something i</span>
  <span id="freeText13698821339882786692" style="display:none"><br />This book has made a splash amongst YA reviewers lately, so I had to make sure I had this read before its release on the 24th. Also, the synopsis saying "24 meets the X Files" made me very interested.<br /><br /><br />Janelle is a 17 year old girl who seems to have the perfect life. Nice, fun job as a lifeguard on the beach, super popular hottie boyfriend, cute little brother and more. She also has a dad that works for the FBI. One day when she is going through his files she discovers a file that says something is going to happen in 24 hours. She doesn't know what it will be, but assumes it's the end of the world and she has to stop it. Ben is a boy from her school that saves her life or er...brings her back to life...after she was hit by a truck. Jannelle feels that Ben is somehow related to whatever is going to happen in 24 hours, too.<br /><br /><br />This is one book where I honestly did not care about the characters at all, and was fully engrossed in the plot. That doesn't often happen to me. I didn't find anything unique about Janelle or any of the other characters, but I did feel Janelle was relatable. She was abused in the past and works hard to make sure no one will ever take advantage of her again.<br /><br /><br />The countdown created amazing suspense and will make any sci-fi fan happy they picked this book up. The story flowed at a nice, fast pace so it never got boring. The writing style is pretty simple.<br /><br /><br />The reason I didn't give this book a higher rating is because I feel like it tried to squeeze a bunch of things into a tiny book and I don't feel much of it will be memorable. To me, anyways. It feels like the author couldn't decide if she wanted to write something totally sci-fi, or maybe a high school drama about the abused teen, or a paranormal romance? I don't know it just felt like too much to me. Others may love the fact that it has a bit of everything to offer the reader, though, so don't let that stop you from checking this book out. This really is a good book that was entertaining and interesting. There are a few parts where you might think "have I read this before"?, because it's honestly got some details that have been used over and over again. I feel like the plot was quite fresh, though.<br /><br /><br />I think the majority of readers who read this book are going to love it! I keep seeing that this book is part of a series, but I haven't found anything on goodreads to confirm that. If it is, though, I will definitely continue reading. This was an excellent debut.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13698821339882786692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_317636870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317636870" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317636870?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stacia (the 2010 club) by: </span>
      Buddy read w/Katy and Anna
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=action-and-adventure">action-and-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=dystopia-or-apocalyptic">dystopia-or-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317636870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8892966882050667932"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Ten days ago, I should have died. But I didn't. I'm alive. I have so much to live for. And this time I'm going to do it right.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><i>Current Status : Happy Camper</i><br/><br/>4.5 stars. It's a miracle! This book is sci-fi but it's not dystopia. You could knock me over with a feather right now. <i>Unraveling</i> is not even technically post-apocalyptic. Think more along the lines of pre-apocalyptic. Either way, I'm in shock. Good job with bucking the trend, Ms. Norris.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, I can't tell you the best pa</span>
  <span id="freeText8892966882050667932" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Ten days ago, I should have died. But I didn't. I'm alive. I have so much to live for. And this time I'm going to do it right.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><i>Current Status : Happy Camper</i><br /><br />4.5 stars. It's a miracle! This book is sci-fi but it's not dystopia. You could knock me over with a feather right now. <i>Unraveling</i> is not even technically post-apocalyptic. Think more along the lines of pre-apocalyptic. Either way, I'm in shock. Good job with bucking the trend, Ms. Norris.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I can't tell you the best parts of the book or I'd be giving away a huge reveal. I think it's pretty safe to say that there's more to the story than meets the eye. Every event is triggered by another event. Starting with the very first chapter...<br /><br /><i>Janelle had a bad day at the beach.</i> Getting hit by a car and being brought back to life by a near stranger was just a small link in a large chain reaction of worse events to come.<br /><br />Ben was the guy who brought Janelle back. He smells like mint, soap and gasoline (we were told this repeatedly) and has a love of fixing things, especially motorcycles. He sounds normal. Oh, well except for that whole "bringing someone back from the dead" thing. <br /><br />Naturally, we're only going to get the information about Ben and how he's involved with everything in bits in pieces. I thought the name <i>Unraveling</i> fit not only the theme of the book but the execution of the plot as well. Everything unraveled a little bit at a time until I was left with an ending which had me excited, yet sad... and satisfied, yet unsatisfied. All in all, it was good stuff.<br /><br />One thing we do find out early on is that Ben and Janelle have a connected past...<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>He remembers everything about me - details I wouldn't have even remembered about those moments - and the way I looked through his eyes...</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Positives :</b><br /><br />The characters. I believed in these characters. They felt like real people who were making real decisions.<br /><br />The suspense. It's always nice to see any love story balanced with some action and mystery. Balance is good.<br /><br />The ability of a story to make me ignore the unbelievable and just go with it. There were a couple of moments which seemed so far out there, even for sci-fi. But I didn't care. I was having too much fun to care.<br /><br /><b>Negatives :</b><br /><br />As mentioned above, there were a lot of repetitive statements and actions, such as the mention of Ben's familiar smells. I'm now fully aware that this author is a fan of the coffee shop "It's a Grind." I shouldn't have been able to pick up on that. I understand that sometimes a repetitive action is used to distinguish one character's uniqueness but it could have been reigned in just a bit. Three times should be the absolute maximum I need to establish that someone's "tell" is tugging on their hair, for example.<br /><br />There were also too many pop culture references. This is what dates a book. If you want a book to be timeless, write it so when people read the book 30 years from now, it still feels like they can slip into the story. Although, I have to admit that I laughed at mention of <i>World of Warcraft</i>'s frost mages still being gimped because that is so true.<br /><br />Even so, the positives far outweigh the negatives. This is going on my list of favorite sci-fi fiction for the year.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>The end of the world is coming. In 24 days.<br /> Stop the Countdown - Save the world.</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />*edit to add one last note!* This has to be the best text message ever in a book. Can you see the innuendo? <br /><br /><b>sry babe get u off tmrw</b><br /><br />Haha.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8892966882050667932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_256396322" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/256396322" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/256396322?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer256396322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11460280606302033965"><b>Unraveling</b> was an action packed story with twists and turns that leave your heart pounding, a swoony and sweet romance, and a smart, likable, resourceful heroine. This fresh and original story was a winning combination for me. <br/><br/>Seventeen year old Janelle’s life has been far from easy. She’s had to grow up quickly with a bipolar mother and a workaholic father. She’s stepped into the role of parent for her brother, Jared and takes care of most of the household chores that a mother would care for, a</span>
  <span id="freeText11460280606302033965" style="display:none"><b>Unraveling</b> was an action packed story with twists and turns that leave your heart pounding, a swoony and sweet romance, and a smart, likable, resourceful heroine. This fresh and original story was a winning combination for me. <br /><br />Seventeen year old Janelle’s life has been far from easy. She’s had to grow up quickly with a bipolar mother and a workaholic father. She’s stepped into the role of parent for her brother, Jared and takes care of most of the household chores that a mother would care for, and her father lets her. She even has to parent her mother who is so unstable Janelle must make sure she eats and doesn’t harm herself or anyone else. In spite of that, Janelle loves her dad fiercely and she has a close relationship with him. She’s always interested in the cases her FBI dad is working on. <br /><br />Everything takes a crazy turn when Janelle is killed in an accident and is brought back to life by a schoolmate, Ben Michaels. Ben has never been on Janelle’s radar when he hangs out with the stoner crowd and she’s an overachieving AP student. But now he has her full attention because she wants to know what happened. As if that wasn’t enough to stick in an “X-File,” the driver and truck that hit Janelle have unexplainable details that seem to fit into a case her father is working on. Then there is the countdown clock listed at the header of every chapter and you have to wonder: what is it counting down to? It gives an urgency to the story as we find out more about it! <br /><br />Unraveling was a non-stop action packed ride, but it was more than that. It was a story of a broken yet loving family. The characters and problems they faced felt real even set in this fantastical story. It was easy to relate to Janelle and all that she’s going through because of that. You experience the sadness of Janelle and her family dealing with a mentally ill and poorly functioning mother. I don’t know how I would cope. It would be hard not to be resentful but Janelle handles things. I think this why she comes off as a lot older than seventeen, and I loved her no-nonsense approach to life. She tackled things without complaining but instead looked for a solution for whatever was thrown at her. <br /><br />My heart swelled over Ben! I wondered right along with Janelle how she never noticed him before. When details of the past come to light you’ll love him even more. Janelle can’t stop thinking about him to the point that another boy she’s been casually dating blends into the background:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>It’s weird, though. As he talks, I feel off—like I’m spacing out. I can’t help but think of Ben Michaels hovering over me, his hands on my skin, the way he said my name. The unflinching certainty I was dead and now I’m not—and it’s because of Ben. </i>
</b><br /><br />I couldn’t stop thinking about Ben either! <br /><br />Ben is all about Janelle too: <br /><br /><b>
  <i> “You’re like gravity to Ben—his own personal gravitational force. He revolves around you. It’s been that way since we got here.” </i>
</b><br /><br />Unfortunately for these two, bigger things are a stake so they can’t just dreamily stare into each other’s eyes and swoon (dang it!). <br /><br />This didn’t leave off on a cliffhanger, but at the end you are anxious to get to the next book. I’ll be picking that up very soon! I can’t wait to see how this story turns out. <br /><br />You can find this review and more at <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2013/03/review-unraveling-unraveling-1-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11460280606302033965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_296469637" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/296469637" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/296469637?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=debut-author-2012">debut-author-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer296469637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1734428303529838734">I think I need someone to explain to me just what was so great about this book, because I sure as hell didn't get it. Maybe I'm missing some pages from my copy of Unraveling, but unlike most of the book blogging community, I was not drawn into this seemingly original story. If anything, Unraveling felt as if it was being written from a checklist:<br/>- Female protagonist who is in high school and has the fate of the world on her shoulders? Check!<br/>- Male protagonist who saves the female protagonist fro</span>
  <span id="freeText1734428303529838734" style="display:none">I think I need someone to explain to me just what was so great about this book, because I sure as hell didn't get it. Maybe I'm missing some pages from my copy of Unraveling, but unlike most of the book blogging community, I was not drawn into this seemingly original story. If anything, Unraveling felt as if it was being written from a checklist:<br />- Female protagonist who is in high school and has the fate of the world on her shoulders? Check!<br />- Male protagonist who saves the female protagonist from death and makes her fall half in love with him through that action alone? Check!<br />- Quiet, shy male protagonist who is in love with the female protagonist from afar and hides his intelligence behind a stoner persona? Check!<br />- Smart, intelligent, popular female protagonist with issues both at home and concerning her past? Check!<br />Practically every standard element that you can think of in your usual YA flick is in this novel, so why was it so popular? Let's see if I can unravel that mystery in my review...<br /><br />When a truck hits Janelle on the road, she should be dead. Yet, even while she's taking what she believes are her last breaths of air, she is mysteriously resurrected by Ben, a stoner who she's never spoken to before. Now, Janelle has to know how she's still alive, why she's still alive, and exactly what her father's new FBI case has to do with anything. There's a countdown and time just may be running out...<br /><br />Janelle, despite having her family issues that I sympathize with, was extremely annoying and her narration completely grated on me. She was constantly whining about her life, taking out her frustration on her younger brother who did nothing, and had an attitude and aura of being better than everyone else around her. If you're thinking she sounds like a bitch you're right! I couldn't stand her and reading her narration took an immense amount of effort. Furthermore, despite supposedly being "smart" and "clever" and "intelligent" she still manages to fall in love with Ben almost instantly. Their love story felt a little too much like Twilight: Edward is mysterious, he saves Bella, Bella tries to find out why, Bella falls in love with him in the process. Now, just substitute Bella and Edward's names with Janelle and Ben and you have the entire romantic story of Unraveling. Unoriginal much?<br /><br />Enough about the characters, let's talk about the plot. I suppose for a debut author, Unraveling was clever and original. Each chapter was a countdown to a bigger event, the bipolar mother had never been done before, and it had elements of science fiction. However, there was way too much going on in this story. There were various subplots and the book was too long and drawn out to be credited with having a tight plot. In addition, I wish that Janelle's mother's bi-polarness had been treated more realistically. It was one aspect of this story that I was really intrigued by and it fell flat. Furthermore, the sci-fi elements in this story were disappointing. Perhaps I've read and watched too much sci-fi for this to come across as being truly authentic, but I wasn't "wowed" by it in the least.<br /><br />Overall, Unraveling was an utter disappointment. I had built this book up to be something amazing in my mind because of all the spectacular reviews, but I didn't find myself enjoying it. I can see the allure for other readers, but I'm getting tired of the same old story lines, characters, and ideas. Publishers seem to enjoy a story that can fit the mold of classic YA, but as a reader, I'm yearning for something more unique. I almost wish I could have seen what other readers saw while reading and falling in love with this book, but I guess I'll never know. I won't be reading any more of Elizabeth Norris in the future, no matter how stunning her reviews are.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1734428303529838734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
